<div id="review_2719593294" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2719593294" />
    <a title="Luna Logan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12892979-luna-logan"><img alt="Luna Logan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516576314p2/12892979.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2719593294?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Luna Logan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Luna Logan" href="/user/show/12892979-luna-logan">Luna Logan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780143112280" href="/book/show/1819228.Londonstani">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2719593294" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4996456134971432293">Londonstani's protagonist feels like an unremarkable boy with unremarkable circumstances. As a coming-of-age story, the novel focuses in on racial tensions that exist in and outside minority groups in London. Themes like toxic masculinity, religious tolerance, and the postcolonial plight blur into one another like watercolors from chapter to chapter. The whole book feels like a whirlwind, so fast and furious, and filled with language you must sound out to understand. The ending catches you unawa</span>
  <span id="freeText4996456134971432293" style="display:none">Londonstani's protagonist feels like an unremarkable boy with unremarkable circumstances. As a coming-of-age story, the novel focuses in on racial tensions that exist in and outside minority groups in London. Themes like toxic masculinity, religious tolerance, and the postcolonial plight blur into one another like watercolors from chapter to chapter. The whole book feels like a whirlwind, so fast and furious, and filled with language you must sound out to understand. The ending catches you unawares and ill at ease. The narrative is slow and the action congregates around certain events, but the novel is successful in demonstrating - rather than explaining - racism, appropriation, and tradition vs. modernity. I find myself stunned by the end. If you’re looking for something different and provocative (and don’t mind reading the book twice for full effect), I highly recommend giving Londonstani a try. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4996456134971432293" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joshua" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joshua" href="/user/show/3797146-joshua">Joshua</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3797146-joshua?shelf=just-because-fiction">just-because-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2871354648" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11681789732542101098">Found this from an excerpt in <i>Rotten English</i> by Dohra Ahmad, a collection of fiction and poetry showcasing vernacular/dialect. This novel does such an interesting job using urban English slang and immigrant Indian and Pakistani dialect and languages. Even better it uses all of that to comment on the role of language in identity and power in society. The first part reminded me of <i>The Outsiders</i> by S.E. Hinton because it's about a tough gang of teen boys that leads to a big fight, but it takes an i</span>
  <span id="freeText11681789732542101098" style="display:none">Found this from an excerpt in <i>Rotten English</i> by Dohra Ahmad, a collection of fiction and poetry showcasing vernacular/dialect. This novel does such an interesting job using urban English slang and immigrant Indian and Pakistani dialect and languages. Even better it uses all of that to comment on the role of language in identity and power in society. The first part reminded me of <i>The Outsiders</i> by S.E. Hinton because it's about a tough gang of teen boys that leads to a big fight, but it takes an interesting turn from there (not to mention the big turn at the end). Well developed all the way through, including Jas' changing perspective on the characters around him like Hardjit and Samira who he initially idolizes and then sees them differently as he evolves over the course of the story.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('MYe6LGOeSQB9W6UW+Q3CzD0uZGHGWsieS34rB0pfAHUa4tKjlv74BJ2VU84v/ffHlgEglVassuPXpuws1B+CiA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xjVZnP1c2+3mdjQX4bCrIAl70wcFMOa0t/3zeI8yZj/tUDETCDxq6Qa4ws83QJ4rolSX85XGnMkrJTRTEXLkwg==')})
  }

Four years later, a teenage Rumi is at the center of an intense campaign by her parents to make her the youngest student ever to attend Oxford University, an effort that requires an unrelenting routine of study. Through the eyes of two Bangladeshi sisters—the plain Nazneen and the prettier Hasina—we see the divergent paths of the contemporary descendants of an ancient culture. Hasina elopes to a &quot;love marriage,&quot; and young Nazneen, in an arranged marriage, is pledged to a much older man living in London. \n\nAli\'s skillful narrative focuses on Nazneen\'s stifling life with her ineffectual husband, who keeps her imprisoned in a city housing project filled with immigrants in varying degrees of assimilation. But Ali reveals a bittersweet tension between the &quot;two kinds of love&quot; Nazneen and her sister experience—that which begins full and overflowing, only to slowly dissipate, and another which emerges like a surprise, growing unexpectedly over years of faithful commitment. Both of these loves have their own pitfalls: Hasina\'s passionate romance crumbles into domestic violence, and Nazneen\'s marriage never quite reaches a state of wedded bliss.\n\nThough comparisons have drawn between Ali and Zadie Smith, a better comparison might be made between this talented newcomer and the work of Amy Tan, who so deftly portrays the immigrant experience with empathy and
